Hemani: \nDear Sir/Madam, \nThe Decision to Move C4W from Faculty of Arts \nI am writing with regards to the recent decision to move Center for Writers (C4W) \nfrom the Faculty of Arts at the University of Alberta to Student Services. This decision did \nnot go through ANY level of governance and came as a shock for both the Director of C4W, \nDr. Lucie Moussu and the tutors because none of these stakeholders were consulted in the \nprocess of decision-making.  \nWriting is commonly accepted as a craft but for the students at the University to \ndevelop this skill effectively during their undergraduate and graduate years, it is essential \nthat support for writing is available to students—and for free, to avoid equity issues. It is \neven more important that these services are reflexively administered such that people \ndirecting and offering these services are academics with due experience and a PhD in a \nfield related to improving the writing and communication skills of all students (especially \ninternational students!).  \nThe Centre for Writers and its placement in the Faculty of Arts at the University of \nAlberta has a history. The decision to establish the centre came about as a result of THREE \nyears of extensive research and consultation (details of the 300-page report can found \nhere: http://writing.ualberta.ca/en/Writing%20Task%20Force.aspx), in which the Writing \nTask Force (which included many students and representatives from across campus) \nagreed that the C4W should be housed in an academic Faculty and have an academic \ndirector. This was approved by all levels of governance (Student Union, GFC, TLAT, FAC, \netc.) and every single Faculty on campus. This thinking and philosophy enabled the centre \nto function as an academic body within the university. It currently can conduct research \nand publish on writing issues, attend and present at conferences, and be active in the field. \nThe current director, Dr. Lucie Moussu, for example, is currently the President of the \nCanadian Writing Centres Association, and many tutors at the Centre would be presenting \nor volunteering at the upcoming Congress of Humanities in Calgary.  \nThe present decision to move C4W from Faculty of Arts was done behind doors and \nwith zero consultation with students or faculty members. How is it that a very successful \nwriting center at the University of Alberta, that has been offering free services to support \nstudents and faculty members in higher-order problems in writing (e.g., critical thinking, \nunderstanding of audience), can be moved to “Student Services” without the consultation of \n2 \nits academic supervisor Dr. Lucie Moussu or anyone else in the Faculty of Arts or elsewhere \nat the university?  \nDr. Moussu’s research in the area of writing center work has not only inspired \nstudents from MLCS to research on this subject but also drawn students from Computer \nSciences to adopt qualitative approaches to studying the writing behaviors of students. She \nhas published in international journals, presented at numerous international conferences, \nhelped build a strong professional association, organized writing centre conferences, \nsuccessfully applied for grants for her work (including a recent SSHRC grant), and also \nsupported the work of numerous writing centres across the world. It is important for a \nresearch university like the UoA to acknowledge that just as writing is not only a craft but \nalso a research field evident through the effective “Writing Studies” program, writing \ncenters are part of this academic milieu of critical thinking and reflexive analysis of current \npractices.  \nUnfortunately, as a result of the current decision, Dr. Lucie Moussu will have to \nresign from her position because of her dismissal from the Centre.  In addition to this, the \ntutors were recently contacted by Barbara Heagle who opened her letter with the following \nwords: \n“It has come to my attention that the change in administration for the C4W, which \nhas just been announced, may have led to some misunderstanding about the status \nof the C4W and its tutors. I want to dispel any rumors or misinformation, and make \nthe situation as clear as possible.” \n     The tone and language of this email is disrespectful to the current director who is \nsubtly being accused of spreading “rumors and misinformation.”  As a graduate student at \nthe University, I find it shameful that the official communication generated by the Faculty \nof Arts dishonors the academic staff in this way!!  \nI, as an international student and tutor at the Center for Writers for three years, \nhave found not only a sense of community at this center but also an openness to embrace \nstudents from diverse cultures and backgrounds as creating a true sense of egalitarianism, \nequity, support, and mutual respect that I have not adequately witnessed at any other \nplaces on campus, especially not the Student Services.  The Centre for Writers is \nincreasingly diverse in its employment of student tutors. The tutors at the Centre for \nWriters are both domestic and international and come from great diversity of ethnic and \ndisciplinary backgrounds---an element that is not very evident in institutions run by \nStudent Services.   \nFor me, the Centre for Writers has not only been a source of student employment \nbut its people and resources are a continuous inspiration to think and improve my writing.  \nI believe that by removing this free service from the Faculty of Arts would do a great \ndisservice to the faculty and students, and lower the standards of student writing in \ncourses and publications, placing a greater burden on the professors to guide their \nstudents to cultivate good writing habits.  \n3 \nThe common belief is that writing centres are remedial places where only struggling \nstudents will go. Research shows that this is absolutely not the case—excellent students \nknow that good writing takes time to learn, that a second pair of eyes is crucial to their \nprogress, and that the discussions that take place in writing centres are critical to their \nunderstanding and learning of academic writing in their disciplines. The philosophy upon \nwhich this center has been thriving is rooted in a body of thinking about the purpose of \nCentre for Writers in the wider academia and Canadian and American Writing Associations.  \nResearch shows that “fixing” students papers will not teach them how to become good \ncommunicators and successful professionals. This institution is not a clinic where students \nget their writing “fixed” but a place of careful reflection and questioning that has \nconnections with thinking in other disciplines of arts.  \nEven though, the Faculty of Arts is undergoing a very difficult moment in its history, \nremoving the support for writing from the faculty will undermine the very goals of the \nfaculty to promote excellence in research and teaching.  The recent announcement by Dean \nDavid Turpin mentioned and I quote:  \n“I am pleased to report that the government is providing stable funding to Alberta’s \n26 post-secondary institutions as promised in Bill 3. We will receive a two percent \nincrease to the base operating grant. Tuition remains frozen, but we will receive \nbackfill funding to cover the loss in tuition revenue equivalent to the annual CPI \nincrease. The government has also extended much-needed funding to the end of July \n2017 to support student mental health initiatives.” \nConsidering this positive increase, a case needs to be made to maintain this center \nfor writers within the Faculty of Arts that was once established through three years of \nextensive research by a university-wide committee, at the request of the Student Union, \nand has been serving students from Arts, Humanities, Sciences and every other faculty and \ndepartment across campus.  \nIn order to maintain excellence in the writing and communication skills produced \nfrom this university, I, as a Graduate Representative at the General Faculties of Council, \nwould like to petition against the recent decision that was taken mysteriously (without the \nconsultation of any stakeholders) to move the Centre for Writers out of Arts and remove \nDr. Lucie Moussu from its directorship, and call for bringing this issue for discussion at the \nnext FAC meeting.   \nSincerely, \nShumaila Hemani \nDoctoral Student, Music \nGraduate Representative, Faculty of Arts Council, General Faculties Council, Arts Research and \nMcCalla Professorship Committees \n4 \nLiaison Officer, International Council of Traditional Music (ICTM) \nRecipient of State of Kuwait Award in Islamic Studies, and the Cultural Diversity Award \n(Edmonton Arts Council) This report \nincluded points on: \n Building community engagement:\no the President’s chairing of Chairs’ Council and Deans’ Council;\no an update on the Vice-President search committee;\no the celebration of the opening of Wahkohtowin Lodge;\no government relations update, including provincial and federal budget briefings;\no his participation in a Northern Indigenous Festival pipe ceremony;\no his recent meetings in the United Kingdom and Germany;\no the annual general meeting of the Worldwide Universities Network (WUN) in The Netherlands;\no a recent Quaecumque Vera Honour Society (QVHS) luncheon; and\no the April 18 Mindshare lecture co-hosted by the University of Alberta and Universities Canada,\nwhere participants addressed various aspects of the future of energy, as well as how our\nsocieties will arrive at that future.\n The Institutional Strategic Planning Process, noting the final consultation process, the upcoming\ngovernance approval path, and the plan’s five themes: Build, Experience, Excel, Engage and Sustain;\n Advancing specific priorities:\no an update on provincial and federal government support for infrastructure spending for research\nand innovation;\no an update on the scholarship for Syrian students, noting that 10 more students will be offered the\naward;\no the upcoming President’s Visiting Committee (PVC) for Faculty of Medicine & Dentistry; and\no the 2016 honorary degree recipients;\n Good News:\no preparations for housing Canada’s Ice Core collection at the University of Alberta;\no accreditation of the Masters of Occupational Therapy (MSc OT) professional program at the\nFaculty of Rehabilitation Medicine;\no the 10 year anniversary of the School of Public Health;\no University of Alberta alumnus Gopinath Sutendra’s receipt of the AIHS Translational Health\nChair in Cardio-Oncology to study the molecular pathways of cancer therapies that lead to heart\ncomplications;\no the newly-appointed GlaxoSmithKline Inc. (GSK) and the Canadian Institutes of Health\nResearch (CIHR) Airway Inflammation Chair, Dr Harissios Vliagoftis; and\no Professors David Bennet and Karim Fouad of the Faculty of Rehabilitation Medicine’s receipt of\na $2 million dollar grant from the National Institute of Health for their research on possible\nmethods of addressing spinal cord injuries by studying the adaptations of neuronal networks\nwithin the nervous system.\n Awards\no Community Connections Awards: Rhonda Bell and Catherine Chan, the Sexual Orientation and\nGender Identity Advocacy Committee, Calder Bateman Communications;\no Alberta Magazine Publishers Association’s Magazine of the Year for 2015: New Trail magazine;\no Government of Alberta Indigenous Graduate and Undergraduate Awards: 46 graduate students\nand 162 undergraduate students;\no 2016 JR Mackay Award (Canadian Geomorphology Research Group): Alberto Reyes,\nDepartment of Earth and Atmospheric Sciences;\nItem No. 22\nBoard of Governors Report to GFC \nC:\\Users\\Brolley\\Downloads\\May-13-2016.Docx \no 2016 Geological Association of Canada’s Logan Medal: Brian Jones, Department of Earth and \nAtmospheric Sciences; \no Honorary Doctor of Sciences from the University of Edinburgh: Margaret-Ann Armour, Associate \nDean (Diversity), Faculty of Science; \no APEGA Excellence in Education Award: Aminah Robinson Fayek, professor in construction \nengineering and management and the NSERC Industrial Research Chair in Strategic \nConstruction Modeling and Delivery; \no APEGA Centennial Leadership Award: Roger Cheng, Chair of the Department of Civil and \nEnvironmental Engineering; \no HSBC Community Contributor of the Year award from the Canadian Centre for Diversity and \nInclusion: Malinda Smith, associate professor, Department of Political Science; \no ATCO Gas Award for Outstanding Lifetime Achievement: Professor Emeritus Lyndal Osborne; \nand  \no Governor General’s Innovation Award recipient: Robert Burrell, Chair of Biomedical Engineering. \nDr Dew included verbal points of interest to the Board on the University of Alberta’s response to the Fort \nMcMurray crisis and its continued plans for the weeks and months leading up to the beginning of the Fall term. \nThe Board Chair noted that he had spoken recently with Premier Notley who asked him to extend her gratitude \nand appreciation for the University community’s response to the crisis, particularly noting the University’s \ncontributions to help accommodate and feed evacuees. \nThe Board also received an update from Ms Heather McCaw, Vice-President (Advancement), on the University’s \nfundraising achievements to date. Ms McCaw noted that the University finished its fiscal year with a $115.3 M \nachievement, which is ahead of the previous year, and reviewed recent successes in advancement and alumni \nengagement. \nBOARD OF GOVERNORS’ APPROVED MOTIONS \nOn the recommendation of the Board Finance and Property Committee, the Board of Governors approved: \n the collection of the Graduate Students’ Association (GSA) Fees and the University of Alberta Students’ \nUnion Fee Schedule 1 for the 2016-17 academic year; \n the proposed Supplemental Application Fee for the Doctor of Medicine Program, to take effect July 1, \n2016; \n that the University of Alberta continue the joint venture (TEC Edmonton) with Edmonton Economic \nDevelopment Corporation, and a financial commitment to TEC Edmonton of $1.5M per year for three (3) \nyears, from January 1, 2017 to December 31, 2019, to fund operating costs; and  \n the Capital Expenditure Authorization Request (CEAR) of twenty million dollars ($20,000,000.00) in \nCanadian funds for a total project cost of twenty million dollars ($20,000,000.00) in Canadian funds for \nthe Devonian Botanic Garden – Development of the Islamic Garden, subject to senior administration \nensuring that all conditions have been met. \nOn the recommendation of the Board University Relations Committee, the Board of Governors approved \nproposed changes to the Committee’s Terms of Reference to reinstate oversight for philanthropic and \nadvancement policies and plans within the Committee mandate. \nOn the recommendation of the Board Chair, Mr Michael Phair, the Board of Governors approved the following \nnew appointments to Board Committees: \n Sarah Ficko, President of the Graduate Students’ Association, to the Finance and Property Committee, \nthe Learning and Discovery Committee, the Safety, Health and Environment Committee; and the \nUniversity Relations Committee; \n Fahim Rahman, President of the Students’ Union, to the Finance and Property Committee and the \nLearning and Discovery Committee; and  \n Colin Champagne, Undergraduate Student Representative, to the Safety, Health and Environment \nCommittee and the University Relations Committee.  \nBoard of Governors Report to GFC \nC:\\Users\\Brolley\\Downloads\\May-13-2016.Docx \nINFORMATION REPORTS   \n Report of the Audit Committee \no Management’s Quarterly Freedom \nhttp://www.governance.ualberta.ca/GFCCalendar.aspx\nItem No. 23b \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of May 30, 2016  \nOUTLINE OF ISSUE \nAgenda Title: Changes to the Code of Student Behaviour, Code of Applicant Behaviour, Practicum \nIntervention Policy to reflect changes in the Alberta Human Rights Act \nMotion:  N/A \nItem   \nAction Requested Approval Recommendation  Discussion/Advice Information \nProposed by Vice-President (Academic) and Provost \nPresenter N/A \nSubject Changes to the Code of Student Behaviour, Code of Applicant \nBehaviour, and Practicum Intervention Policy to comply with AHRA \nDetails \nResponsibility Provost and Vice-President (Academic) \nThe Purpose of the Proposal is \n(please be specific) \nIn December 2015, the Alberta Human Rights Act  was amended to \ninclude gender identity and gender expression as expressly prohibited \ngrounds of discrimination. \nThe attached changes ensure that the Code of Student Behaviour, Code \nof Applicant Behaviour, and Practicum Intervention Policy comply with \nthese revisions. These changes are being circulated for information. \nThe Impact of the Proposal is Ensures compliance with current Alberta Human Rights legislation. \nReplaces/Revises (eg, policies, \nresolutions) \nUpdates the current Code of Student Behaviour, Code of Applicant \nBehaviour, Practicum Intervention Policy \nTimeline/Implementation Date immediately \nEstimated Cost None \nSources of Funding N/A \nNotes  \nAlignment/Compliance \nAlignment with Guiding \nDocuments \nCompliance with Legislation, \nPolicy and/or Procedure \nRelevant to the Proposal \n(please quote legislation and \ninclude identifying section \nnumbers) \n1. Alberta Human Rights Act \n“3(1) No person shall publish, issue or display or cause to be published, \nissued or displayed before the public any statement, publication, notice, \nsign, symbol, emblem or other representation that \n(a) indicates discrimination or an intention to discriminate against a \nperson or a class of persons, or \n(b) is likely to expose a person or a class of persons to hatred or \ncontempt  \nbecause of the race, religious beliefs, colour, gender, gender identity, \ngender expression, physical disability, mental disability, age, ancestry, \nplace of origin, marital status, source of income, family status or sexual \norientation of that person or class of persons.” \n2. Post-secondary Learning Act \n“26(1) Subject to the authority of the board, a general faculties council is \nresponsible for the academic affairs of the university” \nItem No. 23b \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of May 30, 2016  \n3.  Post-secondary Learning Act \n“Student Discipline \n31(1) The general faculties council has general supervision of student \naffairs at a university and in particular, but without restricting the \ngenerality of the foregoing, the general faculties may \n(a) Subject to the right of appeal to the board, discipline students \nattending the university …” \n4. GFC Campus Law Review Committee (CLRC) Terms of \nReference (Mandate of the Committee) \n“A. Code of Student Behaviour \n1. To review, from time to time, the Code of Student Behaviour and \nstudent discipline procedures. \n[…] \nB. Code of Applicant Behaviour \n1. To review, from time to time, the Code of Applicant Behaviour. \n[…] \nC. Practicum Intervention Policy \n1. To review, from time to time, the Practicum Intervention Policy.” \n5. GFC Executive Committee Terms of Reference (3. Mandate of \nthe Committee) \n“Agendas of General Faculties Council  \nGFC has delegated to the Executive Committee the authority to decide \nwhich items are placed on a GFC Agenda, and the order in which those \nagenda items appear on each GFC agenda.  \nWhen ordering items, the GFC Executive Committee will be mindful of \nany matters that are of particular concern to students during March and \nApril so that the student leaders who bring those items forward are able \nto address these items at GFC before their terms end. (EXEC 06 NOV \n2006)  \n[…] \nWith respect to recommendations from other bodies and other GFC \ncommittees, however, the role of the Executive Committee shall be to \nexamine and debate the substance of reports or recommendations and \nto decide if an item is ready to be forwarded to the full governing body. \nThe Executive Committee may decide to refer a proposal back to the \noriginating body, to refer the proposal to another body or individual for \nstudy or review, or to take other action in order to ready a proposal for \nconsideration by General Faculties Council. When the GFC Executive \nCommittee forwards a proposal to GFC, it shall make a recommendation \nthat GFC endorse; endorse with suggested amendments; not endorse; \nor forward the proposal with no comment.” \nRouting (Include meeting dates) \nParticipation: \n(parties who have seen the \nproposal and in what capacity) \nProvost and Vice-President (Academic) \nGeneral Counsel (Code of Student Behaviour) \nGFC Campus Law Review Committee (for information) – April 28, 2016 \nItem No. 23b \nGENERAL FACULTIES COUNCIL \nFor the Meeting of May 30, 2016  \n GFC Executive Committee (for information) – May 16, 2016 \nGeneral Faculties Council (for information) – May 30, 2016 \nApproval Route (Governance) \n(including meeting dates) \nN/A \nFinal Approver N/A \nAttachments (each to be numbered 1 - <>) \n1. A person who has \nnever before attended the University of Alberta \nas a Student as set out and defined in the \nCode of Student Behaviour: (EXEC 04 MAY \n2009) \n  AND \na. has submitted a University of \nAlberta application for \nadmission. \n  or \nb. has submitted any documents \nintended to support his/her \napplication to the University of \nAlberta.(CLRC 25 SEP 2003) \n(EXEC 06 OCT 2003) \n11.8.3.4 Applicant.  A person who has \nnever before attended the University of Alberta \nas a Student as set out and defined in the \nCode of Student Behaviour: (EXEC 04 MAY \n2009) \n  AND \nc. has submitted a University of \nAlberta application for \nadmission. \n  or \nd. has submitted any documents \nintended to support the \nApplicant’s application to the \nUniversity of Alberta.(CLRC 25 \nSEP 2003) (EXEC 06 OCT \n2003) \n11.8.6 Procedures for the Registrar \n(EXEC 04 MAY 2009) \n[…] \n11.8.6.2  The Registrar shall advise the \nApplicant, in writing, by courier or any method \nof delivery offered by Canada Post, about the \nalleged offence, and that no further processing \nwill be done on the application until the case is \nresolved. The Registrar must provide the \nApplicant with a reasonable opportunity to \nrespond to the alleged offence and inform the \nApplicant of his/her right to an advisor. The \nApplicant will be asked to respond to the \nalleged offence, either in person or in writing, \nwithin a time specified by the Registrar. (EXEC \n04 MAY 2009) \n11.8.6    Procedures for the Registrar  \n              (EXEC 04 MAY 2009) \n[…] \n11.8.6.2  The Registrar shall advise the \nApplicant, in writing, by courier or any method \nof delivery offered by Canada Post, about the \nalleged offence, and that no further processing \nwill be done on the application until the case is \nresolved. The Registrar must provide the \nApplicant with a reasonable opportunity to \nrespond to the alleged offence and inform the \nApplicant of the Applicant’s right to an advisor. \nThe Applicant will be asked to respond to the \nalleged offence, either in person or in writing, \nwithin a time specified by the Registrar. (EXEC \n04 MAY 2009) \nChanges to the Practicum Intervention Policy \nCurrent Proposed \n87.7 COMPOSITION OF THE GFC PRB \n[…] \ne. Student and Faculty members who \nhave been called to serve on the GFC PRB for \na particular case may complete their service \non that case even if his or her term on a panel \nexpires or, in the case of Students, a Student \ngraduates or changes status from \nundergraduate to graduate. \n87.7 COMPOSITION OF THE GFC PRB \n[…] \ne. Student and Faculty members who \nhave been called to serve on the GFC PRB for \na particular case may complete their service \non that case even if their term on a panel \nexpires or, in the case of Students, a Student \ngraduates or changes status from \nundergraduate to graduate. \n87.9 PROCEDURES AT THE GFC PRB \nHEARING   \n[…] \nh. SUGGESTED HEARING \nPROCEDURES \nThe GFC PRB shall conduct hearings \nin a manner which, in its sole \ndiscretion, it considers proper. All \ndeterminants of process shall be made \nby the Chair. The hearing will normally \nfollow these procedures, which it may \nvary: (EXEC 04 JUN 2012) \n[…] \nxiv) The Chair shall invite the Appellant \n(and/or Advisor) to present any \nevidence he/she may have by way of \nrebuttal. Such evidence shall be \nsubject to questioning by the \nRespondent (and/or Advisor); \nfollowed by the Panel. (EXEC 04 \nJUN 2012) \n[…] \nk. The Chair shall normally submit the \nwritten decision of the GFC PRB to the \nAppeals Coordinator within ten (10) Working \nDays of the decision being reached. The \nAppeals Coordinator shall then send a copy of \nthe decision to the Appellant/ Respondent and \nhis/her respective advisor, members of the \nGFC PRB Panel, the Office of General \nCounsel, and the panel of AAC/UAB Chairs. \n(EXEC 04 JUN 2012) (EXEC 03 DEC 2012) \n87.9 PROCEDURES AT THE GFC PRB \nHEARING   \n[…] \nh. SUGGESTED HEARING \nPROCEDURES \nThe GFC PRB shall conduct hearings \nin a manner which, in its sole \ndiscretion, it considers proper. All \ndeterminants of process shall be made \nby the Chair. The hearing will normally \nfollow these procedures, which it may \nvary: (EXEC 04 JUN 2012) \n[…] \nxiv) The Chair shall invite the Appellant \n(and/or Advisor) to present any \nevidence the Appellant (and/or \nAdvisor) may have by way of rebuttal. \nSuch evidence shall be subject to \nquestioning by the Respondent \n(and/or Advisor); followed by the \nPanel. (EXEC 04 JUN 2012) \n[…] \nk. The Chair shall normally submit the \nwritten decision of the GFC PRB to the \nAppeals Coordinator within ten (10) Working \nDays of the decision being reached. The \nAppeals Coordinator shall then send a copy of \nthe decision to the Appellant/ Respondent and \ntheir respective advisor, members of the GFC \nPRB Panel, the Office of General Counsel, \nand the panel of AAC/UAB Chairs.
